1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/United_Airlines_%28Continental_Blue_Skyway_livery%29_Boeing_737-924%28ER%29_N75436.jpg/440px-United_Airlines_%28Continental_Blue_Skyway_livery%29_Boeing_737-924%28ER%29_N75436.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="1050" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:United_Airlines_(Continental_Blue_Skyway_livery)_Boeing_737-924(ER)_N75436.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>To commemorate Continental\'s 75th Anniversary, a Boeing 737-900ER aircraft registered N75436 was painted with Continental\'s 1947 "Blue Skyways" livery when it was delivered in June 2009. <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a> continues to fly this retro livery on a different Boeing 737-900ER, registered N75435.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Continental_Airlines_Boeing_737-900_N71411.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Continental_Airlines_Boeing_737-900_N71411.jpg/220px-Continental_Airlines_Boeing_737-900_N71411.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Continental_Airlines_Boeing_737-900_N71411.jpg/330px-Continental_Airlines_Boeing_737-900_N71411.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Continental_Airlines_Boeing_737-900_N71411.jpg/440px-Continental_Airlines_Boeing_737-900_N71411.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1350" data-file-height="900" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Continental_Airlines_Boeing_737-900_N71411.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Continental Airlines 737-900 after takeoff</div></div></div>\n<p>In June 2009, Continental Airlines took delivery of another new Boeing 737-900ER, which was painted with a retro livery to commemorate the airline\'s 75th anniversary. The livery, which was originally used on aircraft beginning in 1947 and is called The Blue Skyway, was selected by Continental employees. Continental flew the aircraft to its three hubs for anniversary celebration events for employees and retirees. Post-merger, United Airlines maintains the livery, but on a different 737-900ER than the aircraft originally carrying it.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> In July 2009 Continental began to offer <a href="/wiki/DirecTV" title="DirecTV">DirecTV</a>, giving customers the choice of 95 channels of live television programming, more channels than any other carrier.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Continental also launched Virtual Expert technology on their website at continental.com, offering customers 24-hour support on the Web for all their travel needs. Continental was the first airline to use this technology.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010s">2010s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_Airlines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2010s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On January 1, 2010, Jeff Smisek, former president and COO, became the CEO of Continental Airlines.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\nContinental also planned to start seasonal nonstop service between <a href="/wiki/Portland_International_Airport" title="Portland International Airport">Portland International Airport (PDX)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ted_Stevens_Anchorage_International_Airport" title="Ted Stevens Anchorage International Airport">Ted Stevens International Airport (ANC)</a>, putting Continental in direct competition with former partner <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Airlines" title="Alaska Airlines">Alaska Airlines</a>. The route was scheduled to start on June 10, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> On February 16, Continental, along with its wholly owned subsidiary <a href="/wiki/Continental_Micronesia" title="Continental Micronesia">Continental Micronesia</a>, announced that it applied for nonstop flights to <a href="/wiki/Haneda_Airport" title="Haneda Airport">Tokyo-Haneda</a> as part of an open-skies agreement between the US and Japan. Continental planned to begin services to Tokyo-Haneda from its New York/Newark hub in late October 2010, and Continental Micronesia planned to start service to Haneda Airport from its Guam hub.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="dead link before (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> However, Haneda slots were awarded to American, Delta, and Hawaiian Airlines instead. Continental Airlines became the first airline to launch a mobile boarding pass service to London\'s Heathrow. The service allowed customers to receive boarding passes electronically on their mobile phones or PDAs.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Continental Airlines left the <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">SkyTeam</a> alliance on October 24, 2009, and joined <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">Star Alliance</a> on October 27, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-StarOct_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StarOct-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Merger_with_United_Airlines">Merger with United Airlines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_Airlines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Merger with United Airlines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines_Holdings" title="United Airlines Holdings">United Airlines Holdings</a></div>\n<p>In February 2008, <a href="/wiki/UAL_Corporation" title="UAL Corporation">UAL Corporation</a> and Continental Airlines began the advanced stages of merger talks and were expected to announce their decision in the immediate aftermath of a definitive merger agreement between rival <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Airlines" title="Northwest Airlines">Northwest Airlines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> The timing of the events was notable because Northwest\'s golden shares in Continental (that gave Northwest veto authority against any merger involving Continental) could be redeemed, freeing Continental to pursue a marriage with United. On April 27, 2008, Continental broke off merger negotiations with United and stated it was going to stand alone.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Despite ending merger talks, Continental announced that it would join United in the Star Alliance.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>United and <a href="/wiki/US_Airways" title="US Airways">US Airways</a> were in advanced merger talks in late April 2008, following the announcement that Continental had broken off talks with United.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> In June 2008, CEOs of both United Airlines and Continental Airlines signed an alliance pact that led to their eventual merger. The alliance was an agreement to link international networks and share technology and passenger perks. This agreement was termed a "virtual merger" as it included many of the benefits of a merger without the actual costs and restructuring involved. The alliance took effect about a year after <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Airlines" title="Northwest Airlines">Northwest Airlines</a> completed their merger, as that released Continental from the SkyTeam contract and allowed for the required nine-month notice. Additionally, Continental joined the Star Alliance, as Delta and Northwest merged.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EM_N71411_(5563088923).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/EM_N71411_%285563088923%29.jpg/220px-EM_N71411_%285563088923%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/EM_N71411_%285563088923%29.jpg/330px-EM_N71411_%285563088923%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/EM_N71411_%285563088923%29.jpg/440px-EM_N71411_%285563088923%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3531" data-file-height="2354" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EM_N71411_(5563088923).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The same Boeing 737-900 (N71411) at <a href="/wiki/McCarran_International_Airport" title="McCarran International Airport">McCarran International Airport</a>. The new <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_livery" title="Aircraft livery">livery</a> after the merger retains the Continental theme, but with the <i>Continental</i> replaced by <i>United</i>.</div></div></div>\n<p>United Airlines was reported to be in serious merger discussion with US Airways in early April 2010. A <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">New York Times</a></i> report indicated that a deal was close. Union consent was cited as a major hurdle for negotiators to clear.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> On April 22, 2010, United announced that it would not pursue a merger with <a href="/wiki/US_Airways" title="US Airways">US Airways</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On May 2, 2010, the Boards of Directors at Continental and United Airlines approved a stock-swap deal that would combine them into the world\'s largest airline in <a href="/wiki/Revenue_passenger_mile" class="mw-redirect" title="Revenue passenger mile">revenue passenger miles</a>. The new airline would take on the United Airlines name, Continental\'s logo and be based in United\'s hometown of Chicago. The new United would be run by Continental\'s CEO, Jeff Smisek, along with United Airline\'s CEO, Glenn Tilton, serving as non-executive Chairman of the board. The deal received approval from US and European regulators in the summer of 2010. The shareholders of both airlines approved the deal on September 17, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters_approve_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters_approve-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Both airlines had been reporting losses in the recession and expected the merger to generate savings of more than <span class="nowrap">$1 billion</span> a year.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCmerger_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCmerger-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August 2010, Continental and United Airlines revealed a new logo that was used after the merger was complete.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Both carriers planned to begin merging operations in 2011 and was expected to receive a single operating certificate by 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-sfgate.com_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sfgate.com-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Continental\'s <a href="/wiki/Air_operator%27s_certificate" title="Air operator&#39;s certificate">air operator\'s certificate</a> (AOC) was retained, while those of United and Continental Micronesia were surrendered.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> On the other hand, United\'s maintenance certificate remained while Continental\'s did not.\n</p><p>On October 1, 2010, UAL Corporation and Continental Airlines completed the planned merger and changed the name to United Continental Holdings. Although the two airlines remained separate until the operational integration was completed by mid-2012, as of that day both airlines were corporately controlled by the same leadership. On Thursday June 27, 2019 United changed its parent company name from United Continental Holdings to <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines_Holdings" title="United Airlines Holdings">United Airlines Holdings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg.com_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg.com-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> On December 22, 2010, Continental Airlines merged operating certificates with Continental Micronesia. All Continental Micronesia flights were then branded and operated by Continental Airlines.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Both carriers began merging their operations in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> On March 22, UCH announced that they had plans to offer Wi-Fi Service on more than 200 domestic Boeing 737 and 757 aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The airlines attained a single operating certificate from the FAA on November 30, 2011. That day, all Continental flights began to use the "United" callsign in air traffic control communications which marked the end of Continental Airlines.<sup id="cite_ref-Freed_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Freed-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:United_Airlines_Boeing_777-222;_N779UA@ORD;12.10.2011_624bo_(6301852958).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/United_Airlines_Boeing_777-222%3B_N779UA%40ORD%3B12.10.2011_624bo_%286301852958%29.jpg/220px-United_Airlines_Boeing_777-222%3B_N779UA%40ORD%3B12.10.2011_624bo_%286301852958%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/United_Airlines_Boeing_777-222%3B_N779UA%40ORD%3B12.10.2011_624bo_%286301852958%29.jpg/330px-United_Airlines_Boeing_777-222%3B_N779UA%40ORD%3B12.10.2011_624bo_%286301852958%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/United_Airlines_Boeing_777-222%3B_N779UA%40ORD%3B12.10.2011_624bo_%286301852958%29.jpg/440px-United_Airlines_Boeing_777-222%3B_N779UA%40ORD%3B12.10.2011_624bo_%286301852958%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:United_Airlines_Boeing_777-222;_N779UA@ORD;12.10.2011_624bo_(6301852958).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Post-merger former United "tulip" and Continental "globe" aircraft at <a href="/wiki/O%27Hare_International_Airport" title="O&#39;Hare International Airport">O\'Hare International Airport</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The new United is the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_largest_airline" class="mw-redirect" title="World&#39;s largest airline">third largest airline</a> in terms of fleet size, while <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> is the largest. The combined airline houses a fleet of over 1,280 aircraft that features a mixture of <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a> aircraft: <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320_family" title="Airbus A320 family">Airbus A319s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320_family" title="Airbus A320 family">Airbus A320s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737" title="Boeing 737">Boeing 737s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boeing_757" title="Boeing 757">Boeing 757s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767" title="Boeing 767">Boeing 767s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777" title="Boeing 777">Boeing 777s</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787_Dreamliner" title="Boeing 787 Dreamliner">Boeing 787 Dreamliners</a> with orders of <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A350" title="Airbus A350">Airbus A350s</a>.\n</p><p>At the time of the merger with United, Continental was the fourth-largest airline in the US based on passenger-miles flown and the fifth largest in total passengers carried. Continental operated flights to destinations throughout the U.S., Canada, Latin America, Europe, and the Asia-Pacific regions. Principal operations were from its four hubs at <a href="/wiki/Newark_Liberty_International_Airport" title="Newark Liberty International Airport">Newark Liberty International Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Bush_Intercontinental_Airport" title="George Bush Intercontinental Airport">George Bush Intercontinental Airport</a> (<a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>), <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Hopkins_International_Airport" title="Cleveland Hopkins International Airport">Cleveland Hopkins International Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antonio_B._Won_Pat_International_Airport" title="Antonio B. Won Pat International Airport">Antonio B. Won Pat International Airport</a> in Guam. The only Continental hubs to be rebranded are <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Hopkins_International_Airport" title="Cleveland Hopkins International Airport">Cleveland Hopkins International Airport</a> and Houston\'s <a href="/wiki/George_Bush_Intercontinental_Airport" title="George Bush Intercontinental Airport">George Bush Intercontinental Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> The Newark hub began the rebranding process on October 19, 2011 with all United-operated ticket counters and gates to be rebranded in Phase One; Phase Two of rebranding at Newark began in 2012 with Continental ticket counters and gates to be rebranded.<sup id="cite_ref-Airline_Spotlight:_Continental_Airlines_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airline_Spotlight:_Continental_Airlines-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> On November 30, 2011, Continental officially merged with <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United</a> and no longer operates as a separate airline.<sup id="cite_ref-Airline_Spotlight:_Continental_Airlines_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airline_Spotlight:_Continental_Airlines-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On March 3, 2012, Continental\'s passenger reservation system and frequent flyer program was merged into United. The last Continental Airlines flight taking off was "Continental Flight 1267", flying from Phoenix to Cleveland, and arriving into Cleveland as "United Flight 1267".<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>United Airlines, Inc. merged into Continental Airlines, Inc., with Continental Airlines, Inc. being the surviving corporate entity and a wholly owned subsidiary of the UAL Corporation, on March 31, 2013. The name of Continental Airlines, Inc. was changed to United Airlines, Inc.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_identity">Corporate identity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_Airlines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Corporate identity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Branding">Branding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_Airlines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Branding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:United_Airlines_Boeing_777-200_Meulemans.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/United_Airlines_Boeing_777-200_Meulemans.jpg/220px-United_Airlines_Boeing_777-200_Meulemans.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/United_Airlines_Boeing_777-200_Meulemans.jpg/330px-United_Airlines_Boeing_777-200_Meulemans.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/United_Airlines_Boeing_777-200_Meulemans.jpg/440px-United_Airlines_Boeing_777-200_Meulemans.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:United_Airlines_Boeing_777-200_Meulemans.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>United 777-200ER in new livery (2011-2019) after merger with Continental Airlines</div></div></div>\n<p>The designer <a href="/wiki/Saul_Bass" title="Saul Bass">Saul Bass</a> designed the Continental "Jet Stream" logo in the late 1960s. In the 1990s, the design agency <a href="/wiki/Lippincott_(brand_consultancy)" title="Lippincott (brand consultancy)">Lippincott</a> introduced the globe logo. Before it merged, Continental\'s livery consisted of a white fuselage, with the globe in blue and gold, and a gray underside. The combined <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a> adopted the pre-merger Continental Airlines livery and logo following the merger.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Slogans">Slogans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_Airlines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Slogans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li>Work Hard. Fly Right. (1998\xe2\x80\x932012)<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>More Airline for Your Money (mid-1990s)<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>One Airline Can Make a Difference (early 1990s \xe2\x80\x93 introduced with the "Globe" livery)</li>\n<li>Working To Be Your Choice (1989)<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Up Where You Belong (1987) <sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>The Only Airline Worth Flying (1985)</li>\n<li>We Really Move Our Tail For You (1975\xe2\x80\x931979)</li>\n<li>If You Can\'t Fly Continental, Try To Have a Nice Trip Anyway (1970s)</li>\n<li>The Airline That Pride Built (1968)</li>\n<li>The Proud Bird With The Golden Tail (1967\xe2\x80\x931981)</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Company_affairs">Company affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_Airlines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Company affairs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Headquarters">Headquarters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_Airlines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Headquarters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chicago_United_Continental_Building_07.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Chicago_United_Continental_Building_07.jpg/180px-Chicago_United_Continental_Building_07.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="321" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Chicago_United_Continental_Building_07.jpg/270px-Chicago_United_Continental_Building_07.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Chicago_United_Continental_Building_07.jpg/360px-Chicago_United_Continental_Building_07.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1788" data-file-height="3189" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chicago_United_Continental_Building_07.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/77_West_Wacker_Drive" title="77 West Wacker Drive">77 West Wacker Drive</a>, the airline\'s final headquarters</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/77_West_Wacker" class="mw-redirect" title="77 West Wacker">77 West Wacker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Continental_Center_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Continental Center I">Continental Center I</a>, and <a href="/wiki/American_General_Center" title="American General Center">American General Center</a></div><p>On October 31, 1937, Continental moved its headquarters to <a href="/wiki/Stapleton_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Stapleton Airport">Stapleton Airport</a> in Denver, Colorado.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Six" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert F. Six">Robert F. Six</a> arranged to have the headquarters moved to Denver from <a href="/wiki/El_Paso,_Texas" title="El Paso, Texas">El Paso, Texas</a> because Six believed that the airline should have its headquarters in a large city with a potential base of customers.<sup id="cite_ref-TheCompany_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheCompany-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ContinentalCenterAtNightHoustonTX.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/ContinentalCenterAtNightHoustonTX.jpg/180px-ContinentalCenterAtNightHoustonTX.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/ContinentalCenterAtNightHoustonTX.jpg/270px-ContinentalCenterAtNightHoustonTX.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/ContinentalCenterAtNightHoustonTX.jpg/360px-ContinentalCenterAtNightHoustonTX.jpg 2x" data-file-width="769" data-file-height="1280" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ContinentalCenterAtNightHoustonTX.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Continental_Center_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Continental Center I">Continental Center I</a> in <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, with the airline logo displayed, and the <a href="/wiki/KBR_Tower" title="KBR Tower">KBR Tower</a></div></div></div>\n<p>At a 1962 press conference in the office of <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Los_Angeles" title="Mayor of Los Angeles">Mayor of Los Angeles</a> <a href="/wiki/Sam_Yorty" title="Sam Yorty">Sam Yorty</a>, Continental Airlines announced that it planned to move its headquarters to Los Angeles in July 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> In 1963 Continental\'s headquarters moved to a two-story, $2.3&#160;million building on the grounds of <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_International_Airport" title="Los Angeles International Airport">Los Angeles International Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Westchester,_Los_Angeles" title="Westchester, Los Angeles">Westchester, Los Angeles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> The July 2009 <i><a href="/wiki/Continental_(magazine)" title="Continental (magazine)">Continental Magazine</a></i> issue stated that the move "underlined Continental\'s western and Pacific orientation."<sup id="cite_ref-TheCompany_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheCompany-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On July 1, 1983 the airline\'s headquarters were relocated to the <a href="/wiki/American_General_Center" title="American General Center">America Tower</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Neartown,_Houston" class="mw-redirect" title="Neartown, Houston">Neartown</a> area of <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, and would remain there until they ended up relocating in 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Map_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Map-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Stephen M. Wolf, the president of Continental said that the company moved its headquarters because <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a> became the largest hub for Continental.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 1997 Continental occupied 250,000 square feet (23,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) of space at the <a href="/wiki/American_General_Center" title="American General Center">America Tower</a>. In addition it had 200,000 square feet (19,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) of office space in a building in proximity to <a href="/wiki/George_Bush_Intercontinental_Airport" title="George Bush Intercontinental Airport">George Bush Intercontinental Airport</a> and 75,000 square feet (7,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) in a building located on Fuqua Road in Houston. The airline planned to move into a new headquarters site; originally it wanted a single site for its operations.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> In September 1997 the airline officially announced that it would consolidate its Houston headquarters in Continental Center I.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> The airline scheduled to move around 3,200 employees in stages beginning in July 1998 and ending in January 1999. The airline consolidated the headquarters operation at the America Tower and three other local operations into Continental Center I and Continental Center II in the <a href="/wiki/Cullen_Center" title="Cullen Center">Cullen Center</a>. <a href="/wiki/Bob_Lanier_(mayor)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bob Lanier (mayor)">Bob Lanier</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Houston" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayor of Houston">Mayor of Houston</a>, said that he was "tickled to death" by the airline\'s move to relocate to <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Houston" title="Downtown Houston">Downtown Houston</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a> and by September 2004 Continental laid off 24% of its clerical and management workers. Despite the reduction of the workforce, Continental did not announce any plans to sublease any of its space in Continental Center I and Continental Center II.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2008 Continental renewed its lease for around 450,000 square feet (42,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) in Continental Center I. Before the lease renewal, rumors spread stating that the airline would relocate its headquarters to office space around <a href="/wiki/George_Bush_Intercontinental_Airport" title="George Bush Intercontinental Airport">George Bush Intercontinental Airport</a> due to high fuel costs affecting the airline industry; the rumors stated that the airline was studying possibilities of less expensive alternatives to Continental Center I.<sup id="cite_ref-houston.bizjournals.com_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-houston.bizjournals.com-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> The parties did not reveal the terms of the lease agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2010, Continental Airlines and United Airlines announced that they would merge and that the headquarters of the combined company would be in the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Loop" title="Chicago Loop">Chicago Loop</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>. The airline has not stated how much of the 480,000 square feet (45,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) of space that it leases in Continental Center I will be vacated.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> As of 2010 Continental had around 3,000 clerical and management workers in its <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Houston" title="Downtown Houston">Downtown Houston</a> offices.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> According to Nicole Bradford of the <i><a href="/wiki/Houston_Business_Journal" class="mw-redirect" title="Houston Business Journal">Houston Business Journal</a></i>, some believe that the airline will vacate and leave thousands of square feet of space in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Houston" title="Downtown Houston">Downtown Houston</a> empty. As of 2010 Continental leases 450,000 square feet (42,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) in Continental Center I, about 40% of the tower\'s office space.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> United has begun to move employees to a new operations center in the <a href="/wiki/Willis_Tower" title="Willis Tower">Willis Tower</a> (former Sears Tower) and one thousand are expected by the end of 2010. As of September 2011 Continental continues to have employees at Continental Center I, which is now a former headquarters. About half of the existing employee base will remain in the building. As of September 2011 Continental continues to occupy space at Continental Center I, now a former headquarters, and another building. Half of the previous number of employees will work in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Houston" title="Downtown Houston">Downtown Houston</a>. Some job positions were eliminated. Some employees were transferred to Chicago.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_record">Environmental record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_Airlines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Environmental record">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Continental Airlines has made efforts to minimize the negative environmental effects of commercial aviation. For example, the carrier invested over $12&#160;billion for the purchase of the current 270 fuel-efficient aircraft and related equipment that make up part of the airline\'s fleet.<sup id="cite_ref-saipantribune_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-saipantribune-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> These efforts have contributed to significant reductions of greenhouse gas and noise emissions, and have decreased fuel consumption by 45% per mainline revenue passenger mile over the past decade.<sup id="cite_ref-saipantribune_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-saipantribune-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Continental Airlines was also one of the first carriers in the world to fit <a href="/wiki/Winglets" class="mw-redirect" title="Winglets">winglets</a> to as much of its fleet as it could, reducing fuel burn by 3\xe2\x80\x935%.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Continental has implemented a program that gives passengers the opportunity to offset their carbon emissions per flight for a fee of $2. Funds collected from the <a href="/wiki/Carbon_offset" title="Carbon offset">carbon offset</a> scheme are directed for tree planting in reforestation areas. Passengers can also contribute $50 or more to fund renewable-energy projects such as wind- or solar-power projects, or to re-establish algae in oceans or large-scale reforestation.<sup id="cite_ref-bizweekbiofuel_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bizweekbiofuel-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/U.S._Environmental_Protection_Agency" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Environmental Protection Agency">U.S. Environmental Protection Agency</a>\'s (EPA) "Design for the Environment Program" has recognized Continental (2008) for use of a non-chromium aircraft surface pre-treatment that is environmentally compatible. Continental Airlines is the first carrier in the world to utilize this technology on their aircraft. The product, "PreKote", manufactured by Pantheon Enterprises, eliminates hazardous chemicals that are usually used in the pre-treatment phase before painting an aircraft. This technology provides improved environmental conditions for maintenance employees, while also reducing wastewater.<sup id="cite_ref-saipantribune_121-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-saipantribune-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Continental Airlines is planning flight tests using aircraft powered by <a href="/wiki/Biofuel" title="Biofuel">biofuel</a> rather than traditional Jet-A1. On January 7, 2009, Continental partnered with <a href="/wiki/GE_Aviation" title="GE Aviation">GE Aviation</a> to conduct a biofuel demonstration flight, making the airline the first U.S. carrier to conduct tests using biofuels. The test bed, a Boeing 737-800 (registered as N76516), ran one of its engines on a mix of 50% <a href="/wiki/Kerosene" title="Kerosene">kerosene</a>, 6% <a href="/wiki/Algae" title="Algae">algae</a>, and 44% <a href="/wiki/Jatropha" title="Jatropha">jatropha</a>, a weed that bears oil producing seeds.<sup id="cite_ref-http&#58;//www.latimes.com/business/la-fi-biofuel8-2009jan08,0,761065.story_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-http://www.latimes.com/business/la-fi-biofuel8-2009jan08,0,761065.story-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> The engine running partly on biofuel burned 46&#160;kg less fuel than the conventional engine in 1 and a half hours while producing more thrust using the same volume of fuel. Continental\'s CEO, Larry Kellner, commented "This is a good step forward, an opportunity to really make a difference to the environment" citing jatropha\'s 50\xe2\x80\x9360% lower CO<sub>2</sub> emissions as opposed to Jet-A1 in its lifecycle.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Continental Airlines has been recognized by NASA and <i>Fortune</i> magazine for positive environmental contributions.<sup id="cite_ref-saipantribune_121-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-saipantribune-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_Airlines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li>No. 1 Most Admired Global Airline; <i>Fortune</i> Magazine (2004\xe2\x80\x932009)<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>No. 1 Most Admired U.S. Airline; <i>Fortune</i> Magazine (2006\xe2\x80\x932007, 2010)<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>No. 1 Greenest U.S. Airline; Greenopia (2009)<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>No. 1 Pet-Friendly Airline; <a href="/wiki/Petfinder" title="Petfinder">Petfinder</a> (2009)<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Best Executive/Business Class; <a href="/wiki/OAG_(Air_Travel_Intelligence)" class="mw-redirect" title="OAG (Air Travel Intelligence)">OAG</a> Airline of the Year Awards (2003\xe2\x80\x932007, 2009)<sup id="cite_ref-continental.com_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-continental.com-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Best Airline Based in North America; <a href="/wiki/OAG_(Air_Travel_Intelligence)" class="mw-redirect" title="OAG (Air Travel Intelligence)">OAG</a> Airline of the Year Awards (2003\xe2\x80\x932009)<sup id="cite_ref-continental.com_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-continental.com-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Best U.S. Carrier Trans-Atlantic and Trans-Pacific Business Class; <a href="/wiki/Cond%C3%A9_Nast_Traveler" title="Cond\xc3\xa9 Nast Traveler">Cond\xc3\xa9 Nast Traveler</a> (1999\xe2\x80\x932006)<sup id="cite_ref-continental.com_130-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-continental.com-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Best Airline for North American Travel; Business Traveler Magazine (2006\xe2\x80\x932009)<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Best Large Domestic Airline (Premium Seating); <a href="/wiki/Zagat" title="Zagat">Zagat</a> Airline Survey(2008)<sup id="cite_ref-marketwatch1_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marketwatch1-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Best Value for the Money (International); <a href="/wiki/Zagat" title="Zagat">Zagat</a> Airline Survey (2009)<sup id="cite_ref-marketwatch1_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marketwatch1-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Highest-Ranked Network Airline; <a href="/wiki/J.D._Power_and_Associates" class="mw-redirect" title="J.D. Power and Associates">J.D. Power and Associates</a> (2007)<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Airline of the Year; <a href="/wiki/OAG_(Air_Travel_Intelligence)" class="mw-redirect" title="OAG (Air Travel Intelligence)">OAG</a> (2004\xe2\x80\x932005)<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Business Leadership Recycling Award; <a href="/wiki/American_Forest_%26_Paper_Association" title="American Forest &amp; Paper Association">American Forest &amp; Paper Association</a> (2010)<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Destinations">Destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_Airlines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Continental_Airlines_destinations" title="List of Continental Airlines destinations">List of Continental Airlines destinations</a></div>\n<p>Continental, together with <a href="/wiki/Continental_Express" title="Continental Express">Continental Express</a> and <a href="/wiki/Continental_Connection" title="Continental Connection">Continental Connection</a>, offered more than 2,400 daily departures throughout the Americas, Europe and the Asia-Pacific region. The summer 2008 schedule saw Continental serving 130 domestic and 132 international destinations.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Continental Airlines operated primarily a hub-and-spoke route network with North American hubs in Cleveland, Houston, and Newark, and a west Pacific hub in Guam. The majority of Continental flights were operated from its hubs, with a few exceptions (Seattle-Anchorage, Los Angeles-Honolulu, and Los Angeles-Havana, LaGuardia \xe2\x80\x93 Aruba). Some affiliated airlines used the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Connection" title="Continental Connection">Continental Connection</a> name also operate flights not involving hubs, such as <a href="/wiki/Gulfstream_International_Airlines" title="Gulfstream International Airlines">Gulfstream International Airlines</a>, which operated intra-Florida and Florida-Bahamas services.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Terminal_E_Waiting_area.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Terminal_E_Waiting_area.jpg/220px-Terminal_E_Waiting_area.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Terminal_E_Waiting_area.jpg/330px-Terminal_E_Waiting_area.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Terminal_E_Waiting_area.jpg/440px-Terminal_E_Waiting_area.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1087" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Terminal_E_Waiting_area.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Continental was the dominant operator at <a href="/wiki/Houston_Intercontinental_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Houston Intercontinental Airport">Houston Intercontinental Airport</a></div></div></div>\n<p>For almost 40 years, Continental operated a very large hub in <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver</a>, Colorado, but took the decision to close that hub in 1995 immediately after the opening of <a href="/wiki/Denver_International_Airport" title="Denver International Airport">Denver International Airport</a> (DIA), which represented a significantly higher-cost operation than the former Stapleton Airport, which DIA had replaced. The abrupt nature of this change came as a shock to Denver, which was experiencing dramatic growth. The void left by Continental\'s departure allowed the establishment of the "new" <a href="/wiki/Frontier_Airlines" title="Frontier Airlines">Frontier Airlines</a> (a startup, rather than the original carrier of that name). Both Frontier and Southwest Airlines (which entered the Denver market after Continental\'s dehubbing) expanded quickly to fill the vacuum created by Continental\'s closing of its Denver hub.\n</p><p>For the first forty years of its existence, Continental was a domestic airline; however, especially after the incorporation of <a href="/wiki/Texas_International_Airlines" title="Texas International Airlines">Texas International</a> routes, it served more Mexican destinations than any other U.S. carrier since the mid-1980s.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Continental first entered the transatlantic market in April 1985, with the introduction of a Houston-<a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">London-Gatwick</a> service. Long prevented from serving <a href="/wiki/London_Heathrow_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Heathrow Airport">London Heathrow Airport</a> because of the provisions of the <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Bermuda II">Bermuda II</a> agreement, which only allowed <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic" title="Virgin Atlantic">Virgin Atlantic</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> to operate flights from Heathrow to the United States, Continental maintained its London services at Gatwick, where in 2007 as many as six flights a day were offered to Newark, Houston, and Cleveland.\n</p><p>In March 2008, an <a href="/wiki/Open_Skies_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Open Skies Agreement">Open Skies Agreement</a> between the U.S. and the European Union became effective, invalidating Bermuda II restrictions that had limited the number of carriers and cities in the U.S. that could serve London-Heathrow. In November 2007 Continental announced that new, nonstop, twice-daily service from its hubs at <a href="/wiki/George_Bush_Intercontinental_Airport" title="George Bush Intercontinental Airport">George Bush Intercontinental Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Newark_Liberty_International_Airport" title="Newark Liberty International Airport">Newark Liberty International Airport</a> to London-Heathrow would be offered; and this service was inaugurated on March 29, 2008. The service replaced existing frequencies to London-Gatwick and were offered with a combination of <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777" title="Boeing 777">Boeing 777-200ER</a> and <a href="/wiki/757-200" class="mw-redirect" title="757-200">757-200</a> equipment, with flat beds guaranteed in the BusinessFirst cabin.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Continental has grown its presence at London-Heathrow to seven daily flights; two to Houston-Intercontinental and five to Newark.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bush_terminal_E.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Bush_terminal_E.jpg/220px-Bush_terminal_E.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Bush_terminal_E.jpg/330px-Bush_terminal_E.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Bush_terminal_E.jpg/440px-Bush_terminal_E.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bush_terminal_E.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Continental operated international flights from Terminal E at <a href="/wiki/George_Bush_Intercontinental_Airport" title="George Bush Intercontinental Airport">George Bush Intercontinental Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>, Continental\'s extensive military charter operations established a presence in the Pacific region that formed the basis for the <a href="/wiki/Air_Micronesia" class="mw-redirect" title="Air Micronesia">Air Micronesia</a> operation. Service to Japan was initiated in the 1970s from Guam and Saipan, and by the late 1980s, nonstop service between Seattle and Tokyo was briefly offered with <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">747</a> equipment, soon to be replaced with a direct Honolulu-<a href="/wiki/Narita_International_Airport" title="Narita International Airport">Tokyo (Narita)</a> flight. Through the 1990s, Continental maintained a minimal presence in the long-haul trans-Pacific market, until the delivery of 777-200ERs in 1998 which saw the addition of nonstop Tokyo service from Houston and Newark. By 2007, Hong Kong and Beijing were added to the network, and in 2009 Shanghai was added, all from the Newark hub. Continental has served Australia in the past with DC-10<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747</a> service from Hawaii; Continental withdrew from much of the Australian market, but continues Air Micronesia <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Next_Generation" title="Boeing 737 Next Generation">Boeing 737-800</a> services between Cairns and Guam on a 4x weekly basis. Beginning in June 2011, it initiated service to <a href="/wiki/Hilo" class="mw-redirect" title="Hilo">Hilo</a>, Hawaii, providing that city the only nonstop air service to and from any destination outside the state of Hawaii.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Continental offered the most destinations of any of the U.S. carrier to India, Japan, Mexico, Ireland and the United Kingdom, and was the only U.S. airline that flew to the Federated States of Micronesia, Marshall Islands, and Norway. Continental began service from Newark to <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>, India on October 1, 2007 making that city Continental\'s second Indian destination.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Codeshare_agreements">Codeshare agreements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_Airlines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Codeshare agreements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ContinentalConnection.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/ContinentalConnection.jpg/220px-ContinentalConnection.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/ContinentalConnection.jpg/330px-ContinentalConnection.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/ContinentalConnection.jpg/440px-ContinentalConnection.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="941" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ContinentalConnection.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Continental_Connection" title="Continental Connection">Continental Connection</a> <a href="/wiki/Beechcraft_1900" title="Beechcraft 1900">Beechcraft 1900</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Continental was a minority owner of <a href="/wiki/ExpressJet_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="ExpressJet Airlines">ExpressJet Airlines</a>, which operated under the "<a href="/wiki/Continental_Express" title="Continental Express">Continental Express</a>" trade name but was a separately managed and public company. <a href="/wiki/Chautauqua_Airlines" title="Chautauqua Airlines">Chautauqua Airlines</a> also flew under the Continental Express identity, and <a href="/wiki/Cape_Air" title="Cape Air">Cape Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colgan_Air" title="Colgan Air">Colgan Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/CommutAir" title="CommutAir">CommutAir</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Silver_Airways" title="Silver Airways">Silver Airways</a> fed Continental\'s flights under the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Connection" title="Continental Connection">Continental Connection</a> identity. Continental did not have any ownership interests in these companies.\n</p><p>In addition to Continental Express and Continental Connection, Continental had <a href="/wiki/Codeshare_agreement" title="Codeshare agreement">codeshare agreements</a> with the following airlines (as of February 2012):<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Aeromar" title="Aeromar">Aeromar</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Avianca" title="Avianca">Avianca</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cape_Air" title="Cape Air">Cape Air</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Copa_Airlines" title="Copa Airlines">Copa Airlines</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Copa_Airlines_Colombia" title="Copa Airlines Colombia">Copa Airlines Colombia</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/EVA_Air" title="EVA Air">EVA Air</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_Airlines" title="Hawaiian Airlines">Hawaiian Airlines</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Island_Air_(Hawaii)" title="Island Air (Hawaii)">Island Air</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/TACA_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="TACA Airlines">TACA Airlines</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a> <small>(Merger partner)</small></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/US_Airways" title="US Airways">US Airways</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a> (<a 2012)</small></li></ul><table>\n\n\n\n<tbody><tr><td></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Continental_Connection_Bombardier_Q400.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Continental_Connection_Bombardier_Q400.jpg/220px-Continental_Connection_Bombardier_Q400.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" Q400.</div></div></div>\n<p>The operators of Continental Connection were:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Cape_Air" title="Cape Air">Cape Air</a> operated out of San Juan (SJU), Puerto Rico to other Puerto Rican destinations, the U.S. and British Virgin Islands, Anguilla and Nevis. It also serviced routes from Guam to Saipan, Saipan to <a href="/wiki/Rota_International_Airport" title="Rota International Airport">Rota</a> and Rota to Guam.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Colgan_Air" title="Colgan Air">Colgan Air</a> operated out of Cleveland, Houston and Newark as a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Pinnacle_Airlines_Corp." title="Pinnacle Airlines Corp.">Pinnacle Airlines Corp.</a><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/CommutAir" title="CommutAir">CommutAir</a> operated mostly from Continental\'s <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Hopkins_International_Airport" title="Cleveland Hopkins International Airport">Cleveland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Newark_Liberty_International_Airport" title="Newark Liberty International Airport">Newark</a> hubs.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Gulfstream_International_Airlines" title="Gulfstream International Airlines">Gulfstream International Airlines</a> operated in the Bahamas, Miami, Ft. Lauderdale, Orlando, Tampa, West Palm Beach, Tallahassee, Pensacola, and Key West. Also operated some flights under the <a href="/wiki/Essential_Air_Service" title="Essential Air Service">Essential Air Service</a> program from Continental\'s <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Hopkins_International_Airport" title="Cleveland Hopkins International Airport">Cleveland</a> hub.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Silver_Airways" title="Silver Airways">Silver Airways</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fleet">Fleet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_Airlines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Fleet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Continental\'s all-<a href="/wiki/Boeing_Commercial_Airplanes" title="Boeing Commercial Airplanes">Boeing</a> fleet consisted of four types (737, 757, 767, and 777) in ten variants, with two variants of the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787_Dreamliner" title="Boeing 787 Dreamliner">Boeing 787 Dreamliner</a> scheduled to enter service in 2011. The company\'s daily aircraft utilization was usually at the top of the industry.<sup id="cite_ref-Scott_11-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scott-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At the time of the merger with United, the Continental Airlines fleet consisted of the following aircraft with an average age of 9.5 years:<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="margin:0.5em auto; text-align:center">\n<caption>Continental Airlines Fleet, September 20, 2010\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th rowspan="2" style="width:150px">Aircraft\n</th>\n<th rowspan="2">In service\n</th>\n<th rowspan="2">Orders\n</th>\n<th colspan="3">Passengers\n</th>\n<th rowspan="2">Notes\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="width:25px;"><abbr title="First">F</abbr>\n</th>\n<th style="width:25px;"><abbr title="Economy">Y</abbr>\n</th>\n<th style="width:25px;">Total\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-500" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-500">Boeing 737-500</a>\n</td>\n<td>29\n</td>\n<td>&#8212;\n</td>\n<td>8\n</td>\n<td>106\n</td>\n<td>114\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-700" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-700">Boeing 737-700</a>\n</td>\n<td>36\n</td>\n<td>46\n</td>\n<td>12\n</td>\n<td>112\n</td>\n<td>124\n</td>\n<td>Remaining orders transferred to United\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td rowspan="2"><a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-800" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-800">Boeing 737-800</a>\n</td>\n<td>8\n</td>\n<td rowspan="2">2\n</td>\n<td>14\n</td>\n<td>141\n</td>\n<td>155\n</td>\n<td>Guam configuration\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>122\n</td>\n<td>16\n</td>\n<td>144\n</td>\n<td>160\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-900" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-900">Boeing 737-900</a>\n</td>\n<td>12\n</td>\n<td>&#8212;\n</td>\n<td>20\n</td>\n<td>153\n</td>\n<td>173\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-900ER" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-900ER">Boeing 737-900ER</a>\n</td>\n<td>33\n</td>\n<td>19\n</td>\n<td>20\n</td>\n<td>153\n</td>\n<td>173\n</td>\n<td>All remaining deliveries transferred to United.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Boeing_757-200" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 757-200">Boeing 757-200</a>\n</td>\n<td>41\n</td>\n<td>&#8212;\n</td>\n<td>16\n</td>\n<td>159\n</td>\n<td>175\n</td>\n<td>All featured Flat-Bed Business First seats. All aircraft transferred to United.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Boeing_757-300" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 757-300">Boeing 757-300</a>\n</td>\n<td>21\n</td>\n<td>&#8212;\n</td>\n<td>24\n</td>\n<td>192\n</td>\n<td>216\n</td>\n<td>Was largest operator of the Boeing 757-300. All aircraft transferred to United.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Boeing_767-200ER" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 767-200ER">Boeing 767-200ER</a>\n</td>\n<td>8\n</td>\n<td>&#8212;\n</td>\n<td>25\n</td>\n<td>149\n</td>\n<td>174\n</td>\n<td>All were featured with Boeing\'s signature 777 style interior.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td rowspan="2"><a href="/wiki/Boeing_767-400ER" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 767-400ER">Boeing 767-400ER</a>\n</td>\n<td>12\n</td>\n<td rowspan="2">&#8212;\n</td>\n<td>35\n</td>\n<td>200\n</td>\n<td>235\n</td>\n<td rowspan="2">The 12 aircraft in the 35/200 configuration were updated with Flat-Bed BusinessFirst seats in 2011.<br />1 aircraft was refitted with United\'s "Economy Plus" seating prior to an SOC.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> All aircraft transferred to United.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>4\n</td>\n<td>20\n</td>\n<td>236\n</td>\n<td>256\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Boeing_777-200ER" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 777-200ER">Boeing 777-200ER</a>\n</td>\n<td>22\n</td>\n<td>&#8212;\n</td>\n<td>50\n</td>\n<td>226\n</td>\n<td>276\n</td>\n<td>2 dry leased from <a href="/wiki/ILFC" class="mw-redirect" title="ILFC">ILFC</a><br />All featured Flat-Bed Business First seats. All aircraft transferred to United.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Boeing_787-8" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 787-8">Boeing 787-8</a>\n</td>\n<td>&#8212;\n</td>\n<td>11\n</td>\n<td colspan="3" class="unsortable"><center><abbr title="N/A">N/A</abbr></center>\n</td>\n<td>Entry into service was projected: Q1 2012<br />Remaining orders were transferred to United\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Boeing_787-9" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 787-9">Boeing 787-9</a>\n</td>\n<td>&#8212;\n</td>\n<td>14\n</td>\n<td colspan="3" class="unsortable"><center><abbr title="N/A">N/A</abbr></center>\n</td>\n<td>Entry into service was projected: 2013<br />Remaining orders were transferred to United\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Total\n</th>\n<th>348\n</th>\n<th>92\n</th>\n<th colspan="4">\n</th></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>By 2013, all of the former Continental fleet, excluding the Boeing 737-500 and Boeing 767-200ER (which were sold, primarily to Russian operators) were repainted in the new United livery, except for the one Boeing 737-900ER in the Continental Blue Skyway retro livery (N75436). United repainted this aircraft to the standard Globe livery in May 2016, and then painted a different airframe in the Blue Skyway, sister ship N75435. The reason for the change is currently unknown to the public.\n</p><p>First Class was offered on Domestic Flights, and BusinessFirst was offered on Transatlantic/Transpacific Flights.\n</p><p>Continental Airlines was one of three carriers (with <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a>) to sign an exclusivity agreement with Boeing in the late 1990s. When Boeing acquired <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas" title="McDonnell Douglas">McDonnell Douglas</a>, the European Union forced Boeing to void the contracts. Both parties had been adhering to the terms under a <a href="/wiki/Gentlemen%27s_agreement" title="Gentlemen&#39;s agreement">gentlemen\'s agreement</a>.\n</p><p>Continental was one of the first major airlines to fly Boeing 757s on transatlantic routes. There have been some instances of range limitations on west-bound transatlantic flights due to strong headwinds resulting in a fuel stop which does not appear on the timetable, but these stops are not common. The use of the 757 with its smaller <a href="/wiki/Seating_capacity" title="Seating capacity">seating capacity</a> allowed for "thin" routes (routes with less passenger traffic) to be economically viable. It allowed non-stop service from smaller cities, such as <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a>, Northern Ireland and <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>, Germany to the New York gateway. Previously, customers originating at these and similar cities needed to connect at European gateways like London Heathrow, Paris Charles de Gaulle, or Frankfurt, in order to travel to New York. United retains a number of these flight routes, mostly based out of Newark, including Newark-Hamburg, Newark-Dublin, and Newark-Berlin.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historic_fleet">Historic fleet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_Airlines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Historic fleet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Over the years, Continental Airlines had in the past operated a variety of the following aircraft:<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="margin:0.5em auto; text-align:center">\n<caption>Continental
