class="mw-headline" id="Cabin">Cabin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_Airlines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Cabin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Continental Airlines had a two-class service configuration, First/BusinessFirst and Economy Class, for aircraft in the mainline fleets.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="BusinessFirst">BusinessFirst</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_Airlines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: BusinessFirst">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Continental had begun deploying BusinessFirst seats that allowed customers to lie completely flat, reclining 180-degrees and providing <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1020198016">.mw-parser-output .frac{white-space:nowrap}.mw-parser-output .frac .num,.mw-parser-output .frac .den{font-size:80%;line-height:0;vertical-align:super}.mw-parser-output .frac .den{vertical-align:sub}.mw-parser-output .sr-only{border:0;clip:rect(0,0,0,0);height:1px;margin:-1px;overflow:hidden;padding:0;position:absolute;width:1px}</style><span class="frac" role="math">6<span class="sr-only">+</span><span class="num">1</span>&#8260;<span class="den">2</span></span> feet (2.0&#160;m) of sleeping space in the fully extended position on its 777-200ER and 757-200 aircraft. The Flat Bed Seat offered a seat measuring up to 25 inches (640&#160;mm) wide when the adjustable armrest was positioned flush with the seat cushion. Electronic controls enabled customers to easily move the seats to an infinite combination of seat adjustments, including lumbar support, leg and foot rests. iPod connectivity was available in the Flat Bed Seat. The new BusinessFirst seats had a six-way adjustable head rest, an individual overhead reading light and an adjustable seat light allowing customers to read in bed without disturbing their neighbor and a privacy shell that allowed for seclusion from other travelers. BusinessFirst customers also received one of the highest crew to passenger ratios (1:8) among all international business class products.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Continental_Airlines_BusinessFirst_gen1_777.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Continental_Airlines_BusinessFirst_gen1_777.jpg/220px-Continental_Airlines_BusinessFirst_gen1_777.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Continental_Airlines_BusinessFirst_gen1_777.jpg/330px-Continental_Airlines_BusinessFirst_gen1_777.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Continental_Airlines_BusinessFirst_gen1_777.jpg/440px-Continental_Airlines_BusinessFirst_gen1_777.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1421" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Continental_Airlines_BusinessFirst_gen1_777.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Previous generation 777 BusinessFirst seats, Replaced in 2010</div></div></div>\n<p>The new BusinessFirst seats were featured on all of Continental\'s <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777" title="Boeing 777">Boeing 777s</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boeing_757" title="Boeing 757">Boeing 757-200</a>\'s. Installation on the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767" title="Boeing 767">Boeing 767</a> fleet was to follow in 2011. The anticipated completion of the roll-out across Continental\'s entire international fleet was planned for August 2012. In addition, all 787 deliveries were to have the seats installed.\n</p><p>Continental considered BusinessFirst to be its signature onboard product, and the service is a frequent subject of advertising campaigns. Customers seated in the BusinessFirst cabin on longhaul flights from the United States to Europe, Asia, select cities in South America, and the Middle East received special ground services, including EliteAccess priority bag service at check-in, expedited security screening (where available), access to Continental\'s Presidents Club or affiliated Star Alliance lounges, personalized Continental Concierge service, and dedicated boarding procedures.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Continental_Airlines_BusinessFirst_entree.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Continental_Airlines_BusinessFirst_entree.jpg/220px-Continental_Airlines_BusinessFirst_entree.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Continental_Airlines_BusinessFirst_entree.jpg/330px-Continental_Airlines_BusinessFirst_entree.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Continental_Airlines_BusinessFirst_entree.jpg/440px-Continental_Airlines_BusinessFirst_entree.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Continental_Airlines_BusinessFirst_entree.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In-flight meal in BusinessFirst</div></div></div>\n<p>On board, multi-course meals were designed by Continental\'s Congress of Chefs, beverages were selected by Continental\'s Wine Masters, and service was provided by flight attendants from separate International crew bases at Newark and Houston. Most flights had at least two meal services. Entertainment was offered at each individual seat, and passengers on Boeing 777 and 757 aircraft had access to a new Audio-Video On Demand system with touch-screen controls. 767 aircraft featured older, looped-video multi-channel entertainment systems, generally with a wider programming selection than Economy Class. 767 aircraft were expected to receive AVOD in the near future. Customers also were provided headphones, a large pillow, wool blanket, and amenity kit prior to departure. Upon arrival, BusinessFirst customers have access to shower facilities and arrival lounges at most airports.\n</p><p>Continental offered a modified BusinessFirst service on flights from the United States mainland to Hawaii. All flights offered the same suite of EliteAccess ground services, along with a similar main meal service on board. Amenities such as pillows and headsets also were the same, but no amenity kits were offered. On flights from Newark and Houston to Honolulu, Continental operated Boeing 767-400ER aircraft with typical recliner-style BusinessFirst seats. On flights from Los Angeles and Orange County to Honolulu/Kahului with <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737" title="Boeing 737">Boeing 737</a> equipment, domestic First Class seats were substituted. Nonstop flights from Guam to Honolulu were exempt from most of these modifications and more closely resembled the standard BusinessFirst service.\n</p><p>No complimentary upgrades were offered to Continental OnePass Elite members on any intercontinental flights offering BusinessFirst service. However, on 767-operated BusinessFirst services to Hawaii, Continental offered a day-of-departure buy up fee for any revenue coach class fare, provided seats were available. Mainland-Hawaii was the only BusinessFirst market where such upgrades are available. In addition, OnePass Elites were eligible for complimentary automatic upgrades on Continental-operated flights from California to Hawaii.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Continental_Airlines_domestic_First_Class_dinner.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Continental_Airlines_domestic_First_Class_dinner.jpg/220px-Continental_Airlines_domestic_First_Class_dinner.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Continental_Airlines_domestic_First_Class_dinner.jpg/330px-Continental_Airlines_domestic_First_Class_dinner.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Continental_Airlines_domestic_First_Class_dinner.jpg/440px-Continental_Airlines_domestic_First_Class_dinner.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Continental_Airlines_domestic_First_Class_dinner.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Domestic First Class dinner</div></div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Domestic_First_Class">Domestic First Class</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_Airlines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Domestic First Class">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Domestic First Class was offered on domestic flights. It was available on all Boeing 737 family aircraft, as well as Boeing 757-300 aircraft. Seats range from 20.75 to 21 inches (530&#160;mm) wide, and had between 37 and 38 inches (970&#160;mm) of pitch. Passengers aboard this class received free meals, refreshments, and alcoholic beverages. Passengers could watch movies on overhead television screens located throughout the cabin. In 2009, Continental began to add <a href="/wiki/LiveTV" title="LiveTV">LiveTV</a> television and <a href="/wiki/Wi-Fi" title="Wi-Fi">Wi-Fi</a> services to all next-generation Boeing 737s and Boeing 757-300s which was free of charge to First Class customers.<sup id="cite_ref-LiveTV_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LiveTV-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On international flights to Russia, Latin America, the Caribbean, and select cities in South America, Continental\'s Domestic First Class service was re-branded as International Business Class. These customers received access to Continental\'s Presidents Club and affiliated Star Alliance lounges on day-of-departure. Also, meal choices were frequently substituted to reflect the local cuisine of destinations served, especially on flights to Latin America.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="International_Economy_Class">International Economy Class</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_Airlines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: International Economy Class">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Continental_Airlines_767-400ER_economy_cabin.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Continental_Airlines_767-400ER_economy_cabin.jpg/220px-Continental_Airlines_767-400ER_economy_cabin.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Continental_Airlines_767-400ER_economy_cabin.jpg/330px-Continental_Airlines_767-400ER_economy_cabin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Continental_Airlines_767-400ER_economy_cabin.jpg/440px-Continental_Airlines_767-400ER_economy_cabin.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2288" data-file-height="1521" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Continental_Airlines_767-400ER_economy_cabin.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>767-400ER economy cabin</div></div></div>\n<p>Economy Class was available on all international flights. Seats range from 17.2 to 17.9 inches (450&#160;mm) wide, and have between 31 and 32 inches (810&#160;mm) of pitch. Passengers aboard this class received free meals, snacks, and non-alcoholic beverages; alcoholic beverages could be purchased for US$6 per drink or one Continental Currency coupon per drink.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> All seats on 757 and 777 equipment were fitted with AVOD touch screen with a wide-ranging selection of films, games, television shows and music.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Domestic_Economy_Class">Domestic Economy Class</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_Airlines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Domestic Economy Class">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Economy Class was available on all domestic flights. Seats were 17.2 inches (440&#160;mm) wide, and had between 31 and 32 inches (810&#160;mm) of pitch. Passengers aboard this class received free non-alcoholic refreshments. Alcoholic beverages may be purchased on board. Passengers on all Boeing 737-700, \xe2\x88\x92800, \xe2\x88\x92900, \xe2\x88\x92900ER, and 757-300 aircraft could watch movies on overhead television screens located throughout the cabin, with headsets available at a charge. In January 2009, Continental began to add <a href="/wiki/LiveTV" title="LiveTV">LiveTV</a> television services to all next-generation Boeing 737s and Boeing 757-300s. LiveTV would be chargeable for Economy Class customers. Continental Airlines offered free meals on domestic economy class flights. In March 2010, for economy class passengers on domestic and Canadian flights under six hours and on certain flights to and from Latin America, the airline discontinued free meals and began <a href="/wiki/Buy_on_board" title="Buy on board">buy on board</a> service in the northern hemisphere in the fall of 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Meal_and_drink_services">Meal and drink services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_Airlines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Meal and drink services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Meals were free on BusinessFirst on all flights.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Flights of a duration of over one hour within North America and flights to and from resort destinations in the Caribbean and Latin America had meals in First Class depending on the mealtimes that the flights are within. All flights to and from non-resort destinations in the Caribbean and Latin America had free meals in First Class, with the exception of certain flights that depart after midnight.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> Meals in Economy Class were served on most flights to and from Asia and Europe. Meals were offered in economy class on all flights to and from non-resort destinations in the Caribbean Latin America, with the exception of some flights departing after midnight. Flights within Asia and the Pacific that were previously operated by <a href="/wiki/Continental_Micronesia" title="Continental Micronesia">Continental Micronesia</a> had free meals and/or snacks offered during mealtimes. Meals were available for purchase on all economy class flights within North America, to/from Canada, and to/from resort destinations within the Caribbean and Latin America if the flight\'s duration is over 6<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1020198016"/><span class="frac" role="math"><span class="num">1</span>&#8260;<span class="den">2</span></span> hours.<sup id="cite_ref-EconDin_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EconDin-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Towards the end of the airline\'s life, on most economy class flights within North America, to/from Canada, and to/from resort destinations within the Caribbean and Latin America, Continental had a <a href="/wiki/Buy_on_board" title="Buy on board">buy on board</a> service. On those flights between 2<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1020198016"/><span class="frac" role="math"><span class="num">1</span>&#8260;<span class="den">2</span></span> hours and 6<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1020198016"/><span class="frac" role="math"><span class="num">1</span>&#8260;<span class="den">2</span></span> hours, snacks were available for purchase, and food for purchase was available on most of those flights that are 3<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1020198016"/><span class="frac" role="math"><span class="num">1</span>&#8260;<span class="den">2</span></span> to 6<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1020198016"/><span class="frac" role="math"><span class="num">1</span>&#8260;<span class="den">2</span></span> hours.<sup id="cite_ref-EconDin_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EconDin-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Originally the airline provided meals free of charge on flights more than 1<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1020198016"/><span class="frac" role="math"><span class="num">1</span>&#8260;<span class="den">2</span></span> hours. The airline continued doing so after competitors charged for meals. In March 2010 the airline announced that it would switch to buy on board for food in fall 2010. The airline said that the absence of free meals would save the airline $35&#160;million per year ($41035403.63 when adjusted for inflation), and if half of economy class passengers on the affected flights purchased food, the airline would make an additional $17&#160;million per year ($19931481.76 when adjusted for inflation). The airline did not say how the transition to buy on board would affect the employment of workers at the subsidiary <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_Food_Services" class="mw-redirect" title="Chelsea Food Services">Chelsea Food Services</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> Buy on board began on October 12, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> On March 1, 2011, Continental stopped serving free snacks on domestic flights to coach passengers in order to align itself with the policy of <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> In addition, on that day all fights between Hawaii, Alaska, and the Mainland U.S. became buy on board flights.<sup id="cite_ref-EconDin2_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EconDin2-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Continental Airlines offered free special meal options on certain flights; special meals include the Child, <a href="/wiki/Gluten_intolerant" class="mw-redirect" title="Gluten intolerant">Gluten intolerant</a>, Hindu vegetarian, Jain, Kosher, Muslim, and Vegan options. The airline offered special meals for all classes of service on flights to and between <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a> and Argentina, Asia, Brazil, Europe, and Hawaii, and the airline offered special meals for all classes of service on flights between <a href="/wiki/Newark,_New_Jersey" title="Newark, New Jersey">Newark</a> and Asia, Brazil, Europe, and Hawaii; flights between Newark and India use Hindu vegetarian as a standard meal choice. In addition, special meals were available in first class on flights between Newark and Alaska, California, Oregon, Washington, and British Columbia. Other routes with special meal service available in first class include Los Angeles to/from Honolulu, Los Angeles to/from Maui, Orange County to/from Honolulu, and Orange County to/from Maui.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The airline offered soft drinks that are free on all flights. Beer, liqueurs, spirits, and wine were free of charge in BusinessFirst and Business Class on all flights, and for a charge in economy class on all flights. On flights within North America and to or from the Caribbean and Latin America, the airline offered "Specialty Beverages" for purchase in economy class.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In-flight_entertainment">In-flight entertainment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_Airlines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: In-flight entertainment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>\n<p>Boeing 757-200 and 777-200ER aircraft included Audio-Video On-Demand (<a href="/wiki/AVOD" class="mw-redirect" title="AVOD">AVOD</a>) in every seat back. Boeing 767 family aircraft were equipped with a personal television located in every seat back, using a tape system. On all Boeing 757-200 and Boeing 777-200ER aircraft, all rows were equipped with power-ports (two power ports per group of 3 seats) that do not require special power adapters or cables.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DirecTV_COA_B738.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/DirecTV_COA_B738.jpg/220px-DirecTV_COA_B738.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="288" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/DirecTV_COA_B738.jpg/330px-DirecTV_COA_B738.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/be/DirecTV_COA_B738.jpg 2x" data-file-width="413" data-file-height="540" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DirecTV_COA_B738.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>DirecTV on board a Continental 737-800</div></div></div>\n<p>Continental Airlines began offering 95 channels of live <a href="/wiki/DirecTV" title="DirecTV">DirecTV</a> television to all passengers on its domestic fleet beginning in January 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-Reiter_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reiter-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> Boeing 737-700s, 800s, 900s, and 900ERs and Boeing 757-300s will receive the service.<sup id="cite_ref-Fleetstatus_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fleetstatus-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> The service became available immediately after a credit card is swiped and confirmed, and could be activated at any point during the flight. Movies started at a set time and cannot be paused, rewound or fast-forwarded. The service was free to first-class passengers and was available for a charge of US$6 in the coach cabin.<sup id="cite_ref-Reiter_168-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reiter-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> Service could become limited and/or interrupted during descent.<sup id="cite_ref-Fleetstatus_169-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fleetstatus-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On December 16, 2009, Continental Airlines, announced that, beginning in the second quarter 2010(see note) it will offer <a href="/wiki/Gogo_Inflight_Internet" title="Gogo Inflight Internet">Gogo Inflight Internet</a> service on its fleet of 21 Boeing 757-300 aircraft that primarily serve domestic routes. The new Gogo Inflight Internet service will provide customers full Internet access on their own standard, Wi-Fi equipped laptop or Personal Electronic Device (PED) at speeds similar to wireless mobile broadband services on the ground. Customers will be able to sign up and log in once the aircraft reaches 10,000 feet (3,000&#160;m). The Gogo system, powered by the Aircell Network and available in the continental U.S., will be available to customers at a cost from $4.95 and up, based on length of flight<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>.\n</p><p>At airport <a href="/wiki/Kiosk" title="Kiosk">kiosks</a> Continental Airlines allowed customers to buy "Continental Currency", a prepaid credit for audio headsets and alcoholic beverages on flights.<sup id="cite_ref-Cocurr_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cocurr-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="OnePass">OnePass</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_Airlines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: OnePass">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Continental_Airlines_OnePass_logo.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/94/Continental_Airlines_OnePass_logo.png/220px-Continental_Airlines_OnePass_logo.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="54" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/9/94/Continental_Airlines_OnePass_logo.png 1.5x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="74" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Continental_Airlines_OnePass_logo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Continental\'s OnePass logo</div></div></div>\n<p>Established in 1987 in cooperation with now defunct <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Airlines">Eastern Airlines</a>, OnePass was the <a href="/wiki/Frequent_flyer_program" class="mw-redirect" title="Frequent flyer program">frequent flyer program</a> for Continental Airlines, the <a href="/wiki/Trump_Shuttle" title="Trump Shuttle">Trump Shuttle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copa_Airlines" title="Copa Airlines">Copa Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/AeroRep%C3%BAblica" class="mw-redirect" title="AeroRep\xc3\xbablica">Copa Airlines Colombia</a>. OnePass offered regular travelers the privilege to obtain free tickets, First Class upgrades on flights, discounted membership for its airport lounge (<a href="#President&#39;s_Club">President\'s Club</a>), and other types of rewards. Customers accumulated miles from flight segments they fly or through Continental Airlines partners. OnePass elite tiers were Silver, Gold, and Platinum Elite which have benefits such as free upgrades, mileage bonus, priority check-in, priority boarding, and much more. Continental previously had a frequent flyer program prior to OnePass called TravelBank, which was started not long after American Airlines started its frequent flyer program in 1981 and when most large United States airlines followed, but this was merged with Eastern Airlines\' frequent flyer program in 1987 to form OnePass.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> The name "OnePass" refers to the ability to accumulate miles on two major airlines, namely Continental and Eastern, in one frequent flyer program.\n</p><p>In addition to its <a href="/wiki/Continental_Express" title="Continental Express">Continental Express</a>, <a href="/wiki/Continental_Connection" title="Continental Connection">Continental Connection</a> and Star Alliance partnerships, Continental had frequent flyer partnerships with the following airlines (as of February 2012):\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Aeromar" title="Aeromar">Aeromar</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cape_Air" title="Cape Air">Cape Air</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Copa_Airlines" title="Copa Airlines">Copa Airlines</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/EVA_Air" title="EVA Air">EVA Air</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_Airlines" title="Hawaiian Airlines">Hawaiian Airlines</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Island_Air_(Hawaii)" title="Island Air (Hawaii)">Island Air</a></li></ul>\n<p>As a result of <a href="#Merger_with_United_Airlines">United Airlines and Continental Airlines merger</a>, on March 3, 2012 OnePass program was phased out and merged into United <a href="/wiki/MileagePlus" title="MileagePlus">MileagePlus</a> program.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> OnePass stopped accepting new membership applications effective February 29, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The President\'s Club was the membership airport lounge program of Continental Airlines.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_Airlines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The following were major accidents and incidents that have occurred on Continental Airlines mainline aircraft.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">\n<caption><b>Continental Airlines reported accidents and incidents</b>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th rowspan="2">Flight\n</th>\n<th rowspan="2">Date\n</th>\n<th rowspan="2">Aircraft\n</th>\n<th rowspan="2">Location\n</th>\n<th rowspan="2">Passengers/Crew\n</th>\n<th colspan="4">Injuries\n</th>\n<th rowspan="2">Other\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Fatal\n</th>\n<th>Serious\n</th>\n<th>Minor\n</th>\n<th>Ground or other injuries/fatalities\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>N/A<sup id="cite_ref-ASN082745_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASN082745-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>August 27, 1945\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Lodestar" class="mw-redirect" title="Lockheed Lodestar">Lockheed Lodestar</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Albuquerque,_New_Mexico" title="Albuquerque, New Mexico">Albuquerque, New MD-82</a>\n</td>\n<td>New York\n</td>\n<td>110/6\n</td>\n<td>0\n</td>\n<td>0\n</td>\n<td>30\n</td>\n<td>0\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1943<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="/wiki/Air_France_Flight_4590" title="Air France Flight 4590">55</a><br /><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>July 25, 2000\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_DC-10" title="McDonnell Douglas DC-10">McDonnell Douglas DC-10</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport" title="Charles de Gaulle Airport">Paris, France</a>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>0\n</td>\n<td>0\n</td>\n<td>0\n</td>\n<td>0\n</td>\n<td>Mechanical failure (source of foreign object that caused <a href="/wiki/Air_France_Flight_4590" title="Air France Flight 4590">Air France Flight 4590</a> to crash)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/El_Paso_International_Airport#Accidents_and_incidents" title="El Paso International Airport">1515</a>\n</td>\n<td>January 16, 2006\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-524" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-524">Boeing 737-524</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/El_Paso_International_Airport" title="El Paso International Airport">El Paso, Texas</a>\n</td>\n<td>114/5\n</td>\n<td>0\n</td>\n<td>0\n</td>\n<td>0\n</td>\n<td>1 fatality (ground crew mechanic)\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Continental_Airlines_Flight_1404" title="Continental Airlines Flight 1404">1404</a>\n</td>\n<td>December 20, 2008\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-500" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-500">Boeing 737-500</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Denver_International_Airport" title="Denver International Airport">Denver</a>\n</td>\n<td>110/5\n</td>\n<td>0\n</td>\n<td>2\n</td>\n<td>45\n</td>\n<td>0\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<ul><li>August 27, 1945\n<ul><li>A Lockheed Lodestar burned out while parked at Albuquerque, New Mexico; there was no one on board.</li></ul></li>\n<li>March 16, 1954\n<ul><li>Flight 46, on a flight from Midland, Texas, to Kansas City, Missouri, suffered vibration just after takeoff and went into a dive; the flight crew managed to make a wheels-up landing in an open field.</li></ul></li>\n<li>May 22, 1962\n<ul><li>Thomas Doty, a passenger intent on having his wife claim money from life insurance, boarded <a href="/wiki/Continental_Airlines_Flight_11" title="Continental Airlines Flight 11">Flight 11</a> with a bomb, which departed <a href="/wiki/O%27Hare_International_Airport" title="O&#39;Hare International Airport">Chicago-O\xe2\x80\x99Hare</a>, destined for <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Municipal_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Kansas City Municipal Airport">Kansas City Municipal Airport</a>. The bomb exploded, breaking off the aircraft\'s tail, and the plane crashed on a farm near <a href="/wiki/Unionville,_Missouri" title="Unionville, Missouri">Unionville, Missouri</a>. All 45 on board died, including the suicide bomber. This aircraft had previously been subject to an attempted hijacking to Cuba, although the hijackers were captured in <a href="/wiki/El_Paso,_Texas" title="El Paso, Texas">El Paso, Texas</a>.</li></ul></li>\n<li>July 8, 1962\n<ul><li>A Vickers Viscount was damaged beyond economic repair when the propellers struck the runway shortly after take-off. A wheels-up landing was made in a wheat field.</li></ul></li>\n<li>January 29, 1963\n<ul><li>Flight 290, en route from <a href="/wiki/Midland_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Midland International Airport">Midland, Texas</a>, to Kansas City, crashed on approach near the south end of the runway and burst into flames.</li></ul></li>\n<li>August 4, 1971\n<ul><li>Continental Airlines Flight 712, on a flight coming from <a href="/wiki/Hilo_International_Airport" title="Hilo International Airport">Hilo International Airport</a> into <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_International_Airport" title="Los Angeles International Airport">Los Angeles International Airport</a> collided in midair over <a href="/wiki/Compton,_California" title="Compton, California">Compton</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Cessna_150" title="Cessna 150">Cessna 150</a> at about 3,950 feet during an evening approach to LAX. The Boeing suffered substantial damage to the outer right-wing panel but landed safely. The Cessna 150 crashed and was destroyed but both occupants survived with injuries.</li></ul></li>\n<li>April 13, 1973\n<ul><li>After bringing <a href="/wiki/Robert_Six" title="Robert Six">Bob</a> and <a href="/wiki/Audrey_Meadows" title="Audrey Meadows">Audrey Six</a> to their Colorado ranch, the Sabreliner crew departed <a href="/wiki/Montrose_Regional_Airport" title="Montrose Regional Airport">Montrose Regional Airport</a>, for the return flight to Los Angeles (LAX). The thrust reverser of the aircraft was deployed in flight shortly after takeoff. The aircraft descended from 1,000 feet (300&#160;m), struck the ground, and was destroyed.</li></ul></li>\n<li>August 7, 1975\n<ul><li>Flight 426, bound for <a href="/wiki/Wichita,_Kansas" title="Wichita, Kansas">Wichita, Kansas</a>, crashed near the departure end of runway shortly after takeoff from Denver-Stapleton International Airport. The aircraft encountered severe windshear at an altitude and airspeed which precluded recovery to level flight. The aircraft descended at a rate which could not be overcome even though the aircraft was flown at or near its maximum lift capability throughout the encounter. The windshear was generated by the outflow from a thunderstorm which was over the aircraft\'s departure path. All passengers and crew were safely evacuated. The aircraft, a Boeing 727, was a total loss.</li></ul></li>\n<li>March 1, 1978\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Continental_Airlines_Flight_603" title="Continental Airlines Flight 603">Flight 603</a> was scheduled to <a href="/wiki/Honolulu_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Honolulu International Airport">Honolulu, HI</a> from Los Angeles. At takeoff, the McDonnell-Douglas DC-10 overran the runway at Los Angeles (<a href="/wiki/LAX" class="mw-redirect" title="LAX">LAX</a>) when the takeoff was aborted as a result of a tire explosion. The resulting overrun caused a fire that engulfed the aircraft. The aircraft was a total loss; two passengers died when they evacuated the aircraft directly into the fire. Two other passengers died three months later of their injuries.</li></ul></li>\n<li>July 8, 1987\n<ul><li>A Continental Boeing 747 had a near collision with an off-course <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a> <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_L-1011" class="mw-redirect" title="Lockheed L-1011">Lockheed L-1011</a>. Both the Delta (London-Cincinnati) and Continental (London-Newark) were heading to the U.S., with a total of nearly 600 people on board. The Delta flight strayed 60 miles (97&#160;km) off course during its flight, and came within 30 feet (9.1&#160;m) of colliding with the 747 as the L-1011 flew under it in Canadian airspace. It was potentially the deadliest aviation accident in history. Delta pilots attempted to convince the Continental crew to cover up the incident and not report it.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></li>\n<li>November 15, 1987\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Continental_Airlines_Flight_1713" title="Continental Airlines Flight 1713">Flight 1713</a>, bound for <a href="/wiki/Boise,_Idaho" title="Boise, Idaho">Boise, Idaho</a>, crashed on take-off during a snowstorm at Stapleton International Airport, Denver, Colorado. 25 passengers and 3 crew were killed.</li></ul></li>\n<li>March 2, 1994\n<ul><li>Flight 795, a <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_MD-80" title="McDonnell Douglas MD-80">McDonnell Douglas MD-82</a>, suffered damage due to a rejected takeoff from runway 13 at <a href="/wiki/LaGuardia_Airport" title="LaGuardia Airport">LaGuardia Airport</a> during wintry conditions.   The aircraft failed to takeoff and came to a stop at the edge of a ditch near the runway. 30 Passengers and crew suffered minor injuries.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_188-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></li>\n<li>February 19, 1996\n<ul><li>Flight 1943 landed wheels up on runway 27 at the Houston Intercontinental Airport, Houston, Texas.</li></ul></li>\n<li>September 16, 1998\n<ul><li>Flight 475 from Houston to Guadalajara, a Boeing 737-500, was damaged beyond repair upon exiting the left side of the runway while landing. There were no injuries, and wind shear is suspected to have been a factor.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></li>\n<li>July 25, 2000\n<ul><li>The official investigation found Flight 55 caused the crash of <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a> <a href="/wiki/Concorde" title="Concorde">Concorde</a> <a href="/wiki/Air_France_Flight_4590" title="Air France Flight 4590">Flight 4590</a> in Paris. The Continental DC-10 dropped a strip of titanium alloy from its <a href="/wiki/Thrust_reverser" class="mw-redirect" title="Thrust reverser">thrust reverser</a> on the runway during takeoff. When AF4590 subsequently departed, Concorde\'s left main landing gear tires struck the strip of metal and were punctured. The tires then exploded and tire rubber fragments penetrated Concorde\'s wing fuel tanks, starting fires in engines 1 and 2, leading to the crash which killed all aboard and four people on the ground. According to the official report on the accident, the strip of metal installed on the Continental jet was made from a different alloy than had been approved by the US <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">Federal Aviation Administration</a> or the engine manufacturer. This led French authorities to undertake a criminal investigation into Continental Airlines,<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> which ended in Continental being fined 200,000 euros and ordered to pay 1 million euros to Air France.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></li>\n<li>January 16, 2006\n<ul><li>A mechanic standing near a Boeing 737 at El Paso International Airport in Texas was sucked into one of the engines and killed. The mechanic\'s failure to maintain proper clearance with the engine intake during a jet engine run, and the failure of contract maintenance personnel to follow written procedures and directives contained in the airline\'s general maintenance manual were determined to be the cause. Factors contributing to the accident were the insufficient training provided to the contract mechanics by the airline, and the failure of the airport to disseminate a policy prohibiting ground engine runs above idle power in the terminal area.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></li>\n<li>December 20, 2008\n<ul><li>Flight 1404 bound for <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, pulled left and ran off of the runway during its takeoff roll at <a href="/wiki/Denver_International_Airport" title="Denver International Airport">Denver International Airport</a>. The cause of the incident is unknown, however the right side of aircraft caught fire once coming to a stop. Of the 115 people on board, 47 sustained injuries, with 2 seriously injured, including the pilot.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents">Incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Continental_Airlines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li>July 1, 1965\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Continental_Airlines_Flight_12" title="Continental Airlines Flight 12">Continental Airlines Flight 12</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_707-100" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 707-100">Boeing 707-100</a>, ran off the runway at <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Downtown_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Kansas City Downtown Airport">Kansas City Downtown Airport</a> landing in heavy rain. All 66 on board survived however the aircraft broke apart in several places and was a total loss.</li></ul></li>\n<li>March 1, 1978\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Continental_Airlines_Flight_603" title="Continental Airlines Flight 603">Continental Airlines Flight 603</a> was a scheduled <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_DC-10" title="McDonnell Douglas DC-10">McDonnell Douglas DC-10</a> flight between <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_International_Airport" title="Los Angeles International Airport">Los Angeles International Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Honolulu_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Honolulu International Airport">Honolulu International Airport</a>. On March 1, 1978, it crashed during an aborted takeoff, resulting in the deaths of four passengers</li></ul></li>\n<li>October 28, 2006\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Continental_Airlines_Flight_1883_taxiway_landing_incident" class="mw-redirect" title="Continental Airlines Flight 1883 taxiway landing incident">Continental Flight 1883</a> , a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_757" title="Boeing 757">Boeing 757-200</a> aircraft carrying 160 passengers, landed on a narrow unoccupied taxiway parallel to runway 29 at <a href="/wiki/Newark_Liberty_International_Airport" title="Newark Liberty International Airport">Newark Liberty International Airport</a> . No one was injured and both pilots were removed from flying status duties pending an investigation. They have since been reinstated. Potentially confusing runway lighting and pilot error were cited in the investigation.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></li>\n<li>In January 2007\n<ul><li>A Continental Boeing 757 pilot died en route from Houston to Puerto Vallarta, Mexico. The flight was diverted to McAllen, Texas.</li></ul></li>\n<li>June 18, 2009\n<ul><li>The captain of Continental Airlines Flight 61, a Boeing 777-200ER, en route from Brussels, Belgium, to Newark, New Jersey, died of natural causes during the trip. The airline alerted federal authorities around 10:30 that morning that Flight 61 was being flown by the first officer and relief pilot. The plane with 247 passengers aboard landed safely at Newark Liberty International Airport at about noon EDT.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></li>\n<li>August 3, 2009\n<ul><li>Continental Airlines Flight 128, a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767" title="Boeing 767">Boeing 767</a>, made an emergency landing in Miami (<a href="/wiki/Miami_International_Airport" title="Miami International Airport">Miami International Airport</a>) due to extreme turbulence. This flight was scheduled from Rio de Janeiro (<a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro-Gale%C3%A3o_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Rio de Janeiro-Gale\xc3\xa3o International Airport">Rio de Janeiro-Gale\xc3\xa3o International Airport</a>) to Houston (<a href="/wiki/George_Bush_Intercontinental_Airport" title="George Bush Intercontinental Airport">George Bush Intercontinental Airport</a>). The plane carried 11 crew members and 168 passengers. At least 26 passengers were injured, including four seriously.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></li>\n<li>December 6, 2010\n<ul><li>Continental Airlines was found criminally responsible for the disaster to Concorde (<a href="/wiki/Air_France_Flight_4590" title="Air France Flight 4590">Air France Flight 4590</a>) at Gonesse on July 25, 2000 (an accident that killed one hundred passengers and nine crew members on board the plane, and four persons on the ground) by a Parisian court and was fined \xe2\x82\xac200,000 ($271,628) and ordered to pay Air France \xe2\x82\xac1&#160;million. Continental mechanic John Taylor was given a 15-month suspended sentence, while another airline operative and three French officials were cleared of all charges. The court ruled that the crash resulted from a piece of metal from a Continental jet that was left on the runway; the object punctured a tire on the Concorde and then ruptured a fuel tank. Another Continental employee, Stanley Ford, was found not guilty. On November 29, 2012, a French appeals court overturned that decision, thereby clearing Continental of criminal responsibility.</li></ul></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See
